< Review>
Awesome place with huge knowledge.< /Review>

<username>Mark Tweddle<//username>< userid>
116644965237714275635</userid>
<Date>1592951437712</Date><GmapID>0x80c2960b38131d71:0x603cee45439b737<//GmapID>< Rate>

</record>
</dataset><record>
<Pictures>None<//Pictures><userid>117474823652012125209<//userid><Rating>5<//Rating>< review>
We've been going to Sego nursery for years, since we discovered them when looking for plants for our garden. The family that owns and runs the nursery are Japanese American and, maybe chalk it up to being half Japanese, I can understand why some people feel like they're aloof or that they offer poor customer service. They aren't going to fall all over themselves trying to please you just because you show up. They're straight-forward, down-to-earth people who can point you at just the right plant for the situation you're looking at.

They keep a couple of cats around so one of their rules is "No Dogs". If you plan on  bringing your pooch, plan on leaving them in the car. And feel free to leave the cats be, it's not a petting zoo.

Also, if you want to bring a sample of a plant for them to look at (to identify or to help diagnose a problem), place it in a sealed plastic bag and expect them to handle it like it's the plague. Because of said cats and other reasons, they really would rather not have to carpet bomb their plants with insecticide or herbicide.

Other than that, they have a large selection of outdoor and indoor plants and a lot of knowledge. They have a smattering of tools, pots and miscellaneous items but their focus is on the plants, trees, flowers and soil you'll need to make your garden grow, regardless of the location.

Often the best experiences we've had with them start with a photo of a spot, a description of the light and water conditions and what we're looking to do. The more specific the better but they usually know what kind of plants will work within the confines of what you're looking to do. If you say "I'd like a flower that's red." You'll get what you can expect from that open-ended a question. If you say, "I'm looking for a plant that can handle a lot of shade but is drought-resistant and has a nice fragrance or can be used in cooking," you'll have better luck.

And no matter what, they'll tell me that despite my Japanese heritage demanding bamboo in my backyard, NO BAMBOO!</review>

One security guard was really over the top and rude to me but the staff treated me alot better that same guard is still there they should keep him outside to keep the loiters at Bay since he is overzealous and could use that energy there. < Text>
I gave birth here in Feb. 2021. The experience was awful.

They ran out of epidural when I was 9cm dilated and I was forced to wait over 90 minutes for the anesthesiologist to return from a different surgery to medicate me. I was told, ‚Äúwell, it‚Äôs Saturday.‚Äù

The c-section nurses were unprofessional and while I was panicking (sobbing/hyperventilating), they giggled and talked loudly about other things while they readied my body for the unexpected surgery. Then they forced a catheter inside of me without medication. I screamed ‚Äúplease stop!‚Äù over and over. They held me down and forced it in. No one explained to me why they needed to do this. It still haunts me. I‚Äôve never lost my agency like that. It traumatized me.

In postpartum care, the nurses were unprofessional, irritable, and forgetful. The bathroom did not have a shower head, so I was told to use a hand wash cloth to bathe myself at the sink daily. <review>My nose surgery was at St John's Ambulatory Surgery Center. Meghan the nurse who prepped me as I went in for surgery was very kind. She explained everything that she was doing and took much care to make sure that I was as comfortable as possible every step of the way. She also called me the day before the surgery with preparation instructions.

The surgery took 1.5 hours. Both Dr Kieu and my nurse each called my wife to tell her how the surgery went (smoothly) and when she could pick me up. Timeline for the day:
- arrived at 5:30
- surgery at 7
- recovery room at 8:45
- left at 10

I had three nose surgeries done all at once:
- septoplasty
- bilateral inferior turbinate reduction
- repair of nasal vestibular stenosis (bilateral) (using latera implants)

Excluding the cost for the surgeon, $12,432.66 was billed to my insurer (includes anesthesiologist, facility, drugs they pump into me before, during, and after surgery, etc). I paid much less than that, but that is what was billed to my insurer.

They tried to get me to pre-pay a massive amount to cover the maximum estimated cost I was expected to have to pay for the surgery, which I pushed back against since the fact that I was getting three surgeries done at once meant that I would likely get them at a discount since they shared 'overhead'. The person on the phone quickly gave in and said 'then what amount are you comfortable prepaying'? I told him '$400' and he was fine with that.

Here are the rev code translations for reference:
0250: pharmacy
0636: pharmacy
0370: anesthesia
0272: medical/surgical supplies
0278: surgical supplies/implant
0360: operating room
0710: recovery room</review><pics>None<//pics><Resp>None<//Resp><Gmap_id>0x80c2a4c558b61355:0x24fa8c430617b226<//Gmap_id></record></dataset><record>

DENNYS IS LIT. the staff definitely all smoke cigarettes and you could tell that everyone in there besides me was a regular to the establishment because the staff knew everyone by name. The food was amazing (I've never been to a denny's as I used to consider myself and IHOP man before tonight). They were "out" of a few things, this seemed to be an obvious hint that the staff simply didnt want to make the requested item (a smoothie) but that's alright. My body fat percentage was happy enough to go without the additional calories and I happily made out alright with a simple ice water. I got the hazelnut crepes and it was no surprise to anyone that the hazelnut was just nutella (that's alright tho, I loved it). Basically, my takeaway here is that this place is exactly what you would expect, a fairly low budget seat-in, breakfast and pancake place where the staff is friendly enough, the atmosphere warm enough and the food, good enough. < Rate>
4</Rate>
< text>
I hadn't eaten in a Denny's in 10 years and was surprised that the food actually was pretty good. I got some sort of bourbon chicken skillet which was basically french fries and some peppers with sweet Szechuan sauce served on a hot Skillet under a couple of chicken breasts. Very not upscale but tasty and I wasn't real picky arriving in town close to midnight after a long day on the road.

The restaurant ambience was non-existent as you would expect of a Denny's, though the staffers were acceptable and quite busy with a large crowd. They were polite even as they had to throw some trashy woman out for smoking pot in the bathroom.

Parking lot looks a little sketchy when you leave, dark in a corner and I couldn't tell if the woman out front was a prostitute or a panhandler or both... But she seemed harmless and didn't bother me once I walked by.< /text>
